Al-Bayhaqi's Commentary: Imam al-Ash'ari as the Reviver of Sunnah
Al-Bayhaqi's commentary applying hadith to Imam al-Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bayhaqi's application of the hadith to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, highlighting his role in defending Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
Al-Bayhaqi saw Imam al-Ash'ari as the perfect embodiment of the praised community.

In this commentary, the renowned hadith scholar al-Bayhaqi directly links the prophetic praise to Imam al-Ash'ari, explaining his unique contribution to theology. He emphasizes that Imam al-Ash'ari was specially chosen to strengthen the Sunnah and refute innovations.

Guided Path
1
Read Bayhaqi's commentary
Read the Arabic passage from al-Bayhaqi's statement. Note how he transitions from the hadith to praising Imam al-Ash'ari.
2
Note the specific qualities
Identify the phrases: 'تقوية السنة وقمع البدعة' (strengthening Sunnah, suppressing innovation) and 'باظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة' (manifesting proof, refuting doubts). These define his role.
3
Understand the condition
Bayhaqi states that anyone who follows the path of Abu Musa in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community. This extends the praise to followers of the Ash'ari school.
This is the key theological takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله الحافظ ثنا أبو العباس محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب بن جرير وأبو عامر العقدى قالا ثنا شعبة عن سماك واخبرنا أبو بكر عبدالغفار بن محمد بن الحسين الشيروى فى كتابه وحدثني أبو المحاسن عبد الرزاق بن محمد بن ابي نصر الطبسى بنيسابور عنه قال أنبا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسن الحيرى ثنا محمد بن يعقوب ثنا ابراهيم بن مرزوق ثنا وهب عن شعبة قال وثنا ابراهيم ثنا أبو عامر عن شعبة عن سماك بن حرب عن عياض الأشعرى قال لما نزلت (فسوف يأتي الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) أومأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أبي موسى رضى الله عنه فقال (هم قوم هذا) قال البيهقى وذلك لما وجد فيه من الفضيلة الجليلة والرتبة الشريفة للامام ابي الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه فهو من قوم أبي موسى وأولاده الذين أوتوا العلم ورزقوا الفهم مخصوصا من بينهم بتقوية السنة وقمع البدعة باظهار الحجة ورد الشبهة، والأشبه ان يكون رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم انما جعل قوم ابى موسى من قوم يحبهم الله ويحبونه، لما علم من صحة دينهم وعرف من قوة يقينهم فمن نحا في علم الأصول نحوهم وتبع فى نفى التشبيه مع ملازمة الكتاب والسنة قولهم جعل من جملتهم وعد من حسابهم بمشيئة الله واذنه اعاننا الله تعالى على ذلك بمنه وختم بالسعادة والشهادة بجوده وليعلم المنصف من اصحابنا صنع الله تعالى في تقديم هذا الأصل الشريف لما ذخر لعباده من هذا الفرع المنيف الذي أحيا به السنة وامات به البدعة، وجعله خلف حق لسلف صدق، أخبرنا أبو الفتح محمد بن علی بن عبدالله المصرى وأبو بكر ناصر بن ابی العباس بن على الصيدلاني بهراه قالا أنبا محمد بن عبد العزيز الفارسي أنبا عبدالرحمن بن أحمد بن ابی شریح قال نا يحيى بن محمد بن صاعد ثنا أبو سعيد الأشج ثنا عبد الله بن ادريس عن ليث عن مجاهد في قوله عز وجل (فسوف يأتى الله بقوم يحبهم ويحبونه) قال قوم سبا والأشعريون قوم من سبا واكرم بذلك اصلا ونسبا .
Abd Allah al-Hafiz narrated to us from Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb ibn Jarir and Abu 'Amir al-'Aqadi from Shu'bah from Simak; and Abu Bakr 'Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Shirawayh informed us in his book, and Abu al-Mahasin 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr al-Tabasi informed me from him from Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Hasan al-Hayri from Muhammad ibn Ya'qub from Ibrahim ibn Marzuq from Wahb from Shu'bah, and Ibrahim narrated to us from Abu 'Amir from Shu'bah from Simak ibn Harb from 'Iyad al-Ash'ari who said: When the verse was revealed, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him," the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) and said, "They are the people of this one." Al-Bayhaqi said: That is because of the great virtue and noble rank that he (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari) possessed. So he is from the people of Abu Musa and his descendants who were given knowledge and granted understanding, singled out among them for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts. It is most likely that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made the people of Abu Musa among the people whom Allah loves and who love Him because He knew the soundness of their religion and recognized the strength of their certainty. So whoever pursues the path of the people of Abu Musa in the science of principles (usul) and follows their statement in negating anthropomorphism while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is counted among them and reckoned with them, by the will and permission of Allah. May Allah help us to that by His grace and seal it with happiness and martyrdom by His bounty. And let the fair-minded among our companions know the act of Allah in presenting this noble origin, for what He has stored for His servants from this lofty branch through which He revived the Sunnah and killed innovation, and made it a true successor to a truthful predecessor. Abu al-Fath Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd Allah al-Misri and Abu Bakr Nasir ibn Abi al-'Abbas ibn 'Ali al-Saydalani in Herat informed us both, saying: Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farisi informed us from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Shuraih from Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id from Abu Sa'id al-Ashajj from 'Abd Allah ibn Idris from Layth from Mujahid regarding the saying of Allah Almighty, "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him": He said: They are the people of Saba', and the Ash'aris are a people from Saba' — how noble is that origin and lineage!
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a combined narration and commentary. It begins with a hadith narrated by 'Iyad al-Ash'ari: when the Quranic verse "Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and who love Him" (Quran 5:54) was revealed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) pointed to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and said, "They are the people of this one." This establishes a prophetic praise for the Ash'ari tribe. Al-Bayhaqi then comments, applying this praise specifically to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, the founder of the Ash'ari school, because of his great virtue and noble rank. He explains that Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is from the people of Abu Musa, meaning he inherits that praise. Bayhaqi then elaborates that among the descendants of Abu Musa, Abu al-Hasan was specially distinguished for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation through clear proofs and refutation of doubts. The passage then gives a reason why the Prophet (peace be upon him) designated the people of Abu Musa: Allah knew the soundness of their faith and the strength of their certainty. Therefore, anyone who follows their path in the science of theological principles (usul) and in negating anthropomorphism (tashbih) while adhering to the Book and Sunnah is considered among them. The passage ends with a separate chain from Mujahid, who interprets the verse as referring to the people of Saba', and notes that the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus linking them to the praised community. The entire section serves to elevate the Ash'ari school by connecting it to prophetic praise and Quranic interpretation.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
نفي التشبيه
أصول
السنة
البدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what was Imam al-Ash'ari's special role among the descendants of Abu Musa?
A) He was the most knowledgeable in jurisprudence
B) He was singled out for strengthening the Sunnah and suppressing innovation by manifesting proof and refuting doubts
C) He was the wealthiest scholar of his time
D) He was the only one who memorized the Quran

Key Takeaway
Al-Bayhaqi shows that anyone who follows the Ash'ari path in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you someone who loves the People of the Sunnah because of their adherence to the Book and Sunnah, or do you find yourself critical of them? Are you willing to examine your heart and see if you truly love those whom Allah loves?
?
Bayhaqi says that anyone who follows the Ash'ari path in usul and negation of tashbih is counted among the beloved community. If you claim to follow this path, do your daily actions and intellectual pursuits reflect a genuine defense of the Sunnah and rejection of innovation, or is it just a label?
?
The Prophet praised the people of Abu Musa for their sound religion and strong certainty. How certain are you in your own beliefs? Are you willing to devote effort to strengthen your faith through study of usul, or do you remain passive?

The Ash'ari Lineage: From Saba' to Prophetic Praise
Narration from Mujahid linking the verse to Saba' and Ash'aris

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the connection between the Ash'aris, the people of Saba', and the Quranic verse, as narrated from the early scholar Mujahid.

Core Idea
The Ash'aris trace their blessed lineage back to Saba', a people mentioned in the Quran.

This lesson presents a separate interpretation from the early scholar Mujahid, who identifies the beloved community in the verse as the people of Saba', and notes that the Ash'aris are from Saba', thus reinforcing their honored status from a different angle.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration from Mujahid
Read the Arabic chain and the statement of Mujahid. Note that he interprets 'people whom Allah loves' as the people of Saba'.
This is a tafsir narration.
2
Reflect on the dual honor
The Ash'aris are not only praised by the Prophet but also linked to a Quranically honored people (Saba'). This adds a layer of prestige.

Hadith of the Renewer Every Hundred Years and Early Mujaddids
Hadith and identification of first two mujaddids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith promising a renewer every century and the early scholarly identification of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the first two mujaddids.

Core Idea
Allah sends a renewer for this ummah every century.

This lesson presents a key hadith that promises religious renewal at the start of each century. We will read the hadith as transmitted by Abu Dawud and others, and see how early scholars identified the first two renewers: 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the Arabic hadith carefully, noting its promise that Allah will send a renewer every hundred years.
The hadith is attributed to Abu Hurayrah and is considered authentic.
2
Understand 'renewal of religion'
Reflect on what 'tajdid al-din' means: reviving and purifying the faith, not introducing new doctrines.
3
Identify the first two mujaddids
Note the early authorities' identification: 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz for the first century and Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i for the second.
These identifications are based on the hadith and scholarly consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اخبرنا الشيخان أبو القسم عبدالملك بن عبد الله بن داود المغربي وأبو غالب محمد بن الحسن بن على البصرى الماوردى ببغداد قالا أنبا أبو على على بن أحمد بن على التسترى بالبصرة ثنا القاضي الشريف أبو عمر أحمد بن القسم بن جعفر بن عبد الواحد الهاشمي، ثنا أبو على محمد بن عمرو اللؤلؤى ثنا أبو داود سليمان بن الاشعث السجستاني في كتاب السنن قال ثنا سليمان بن داود المهرى أنبا ابن وهب اخبرنی سعید بن ابی ايوب عن شراحيل بن يزيد المعافري عن ابي علقمة عن ابي هريرة فيما أعلم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( ان الله عز وجل يبعث لهذه الأمة على رأس كل مائة سنة من يجدد لها دينها قال أبو داود رواه الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن شريح الاسكندرانى لم يخبر به شراحيل اخبرناه الشيخ أبو القسم اسماعيل بن أحمد بن السمرقندى انا أبو القسم اسماعيل بن مسعدة الجرجاني ببغداد انا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمى انا أبو أحمد عبد الله بن عدى الجرجانى انا العباس بن محمد بن العباس البصري والقسم بن عبد الله بن مهدی نا حميم قالا نا عمرو بن سواد السرحي ح قال أبو أحمد بن عدى ونا يحيى بن محمد بن يحيى بن اخي حرملة بن یحيى نا عمى حرملة بن يحيى ح قال أبو أحمد وانا محمد بن هرون بن حسان ومحمد بن علی بن الحسين قالا نا أحمد بن عبدالرحمن بن وهب قالوا ثنا ابن وهب قال حدثني سعيد بن أبى ايوب عن شراحيل بن يزيد المعافري عن أبي علقمة عن ابي هريرة فيما أعلم عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ( ان الله يبعث لهذه الأمة على رأس كل مائة سنة من يجدد لها دينها ) . قال محمد بن علی بن الحسين سمعت أصحابنا يقولون كان في المائة الأولى عمر بن عبد العزيز وفى المائة الثانية محمد بن ادريس الشافعي رحمة عليهما
The two shaykhs, Abu al-Qasim 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Dawud al-Maghribi and Abu Ghalib Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Basri al-Mawardi in Baghdad, informed us both, saying: Abu 'Ali 'Ali ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ali al-Tustari in Basra informed us from the noble judge Abu 'Umar Ahmad ibn al-Qasim ibn Ja'far ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Hashimi from Abu 'Ali Muhammad ibn 'Amr al-Lu'lu'i from Abu Dawud Sulayman ibn al-Ash'ath al-Sijistani in the Book of Sunan from Sulayman ibn Dawud al-Mahri from Ibn Wahb from Sa'id ibn Abi Ayyub from Sharahil ibn Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqamah from Abu Hurayrah — as far as I know — from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: "Indeed, Allah Almighty will send for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew for it its religion." Abu Dawud said: It was narrated by Shaykh 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Shuraih al-Iskandarani but he did not report it from Sharahil. It was narrated to us by Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi from Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'adah al-Jurjani in Baghdad from Abu al-Qasim Hamzah ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi from Abu Ahmad 'Abd Allah ibn 'Adi al-Jurjani from al-'Abbas ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Basri and al-Qasim ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Mahdi from Humaym from 'Amr ibn Sawwad al-Sarhi; and Abu Ahmad ibn 'Adi narrated to us from Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Akhi Harmalah ibn Yahya from my uncle Harmalah ibn Yahya; and Abu Ahmad narrated to us from Muhammad ibn Harun ibn Hassan and Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn from Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Wahb from Ibn Wahb from Sa'id ibn Abi Ayyub from Sharahil ibn Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqamah from Abu Hurayrah — as far as I know — from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: "Indeed, Allah sends for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew for it its religion." Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn said: I heard our companions say: In the first century it was 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, and in the second century it was Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i — may Allah have mercy on them both.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a hadith report with multiple chains of transmission, followed by an identification of the early renewers. The primary hadith, from Abu Hurayrah, states that Allah sends for the Muslim community (ummah) at the beginning of every hundred years someone who will renew (yujaddid) the religion. The text includes two parallel chains via Abu Dawud and others to establish the hadith's authenticity. After the hadith, the narrator Muhammad ibn 'Ali ibn al-Husayn (likely the son of Imam al-Husayn) reports that the early authorities (aṣḥābinā) identified the first-century renewer as 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz (the Umayyad caliph known for his piety and reforms) and the second-century renewer as Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i (the founder of the Shafi'i school of law). This passage thus provides both the textual basis for the concept of tajdid (renewal) and early examples of who fulfilled that role. The multiple chains emphasize the reliability of the hadith, while the identification shows how early scholars understood and applied the prophecy.

عمر بن عبد العزيز
محمد بن إدريس الشافعي
رأس كل مائة سنة
أبو داود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means exactly one renewer is sent every century and no more.
Correction: The hadith is a general promise that renewal will occur, not that there is only one renewer per century or that every century has a single identifiable figure.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who were identified as the renewers (mujaddids) for the first and second centuries?
A) Abu Bakr and 'Umar
B) 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i
C) Abu Hanifah and Malik ibn Anas
D) Ahmad ibn Hanbal and al-Ash'ari

Key Takeaway
The hadith promises renewal every century, and early scholars identified 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the first two renewers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to rely on the scholars of the past, or are you actively seeking to be part of the ongoing renewal of this religion? What is one action you can take today to embody the spirit of tajdid?
?
If Allah sent a renewer in every century, what does that imply about your own responsibility to learn and revive your faith? Will you wait for others or take the first step yourself?

Imam Ahmad's Praise for al-Shafi'i and the Hadith on Qurayshi Scholars
Ibn 'Asakir quotes Imam Ahmad deferring to al-Shafi'i and a hadith about a scholar from Quraysh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context and significance of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's deference to Imam al-Shafi'i and the prophetic hadith about a Qurayshi scholar.

Core Idea
Imam Ahmad relied on al-Shafi'i when lacking textual evidence, because he was a Qurayshi scholar whose knowledge would fill the earth.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work provides a fascinating glimpse into the relationship between two of the greatest early Sunni imams: Ahmad ibn Hanbal and al-Shafi'i. It shows Ahmad's profound respect for al-Shafi'i's scholarship, even as an imam of his own school. The lesson will examine the report, the hadith cited, and the implications for understanding how early scholars viewed authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Note the chain of transmission and the core statement.
The text ends abruptly; focus on the part we have.
2
Identify the chain of transmission
Trace the isnad from al-Marwarrudhi back to the Prophet (SAW) for the hadith. Notice the sequence of narrators.
This shows the care early scholars took in preserving reports.
3
Analyze Ahmad's statement
What did Ahmad say he does when faced with a question for which he knows no 'khabar'? Why does he rely on al-Shafi'i?
Ahmad's reason is that al-Shafi'i is a Qurayshi imam.
4
Connect to the hadith
How does the hadith about a Qurayshi scholar support Ahmad's deference? Discuss the link between the hadith and al-Shafi'i.
The hadith is a promise that a Qurayshi scholar will spread knowledge.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
Some think Ahmad always followed al-Shafi'i. Read the statement again: it's specifically when he lacks textual evidence.
This humility reflects the methodology of early imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اخبرنا الشيخ أبو المعالي محمد بن اسماعيل بن محمد بن الحسين الفارسي بنيسابور انا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن على البيهقى انا أبو عبدالرحمن محمد بن الحسين السلمى نا أبو عبد الله محمد بن العباس العصمى نا أبو اسحق أحمد بن محمد بن ياسين الهروي قال سمعت ابراهيم بن اسحاق الانصارى يقول سمعت المروروذی صاحب احمد بن حنبل يقول قال احمد : إذا سألت عن مسألة لا أعلم فيها خبرا قلت فيها يقول الشافعي لانه امام عالم من قریش وروى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انه قال ( عالم قريش يملأ الأرض علما وذكر في الخبر ان الله يقيض عليه
The shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Farisi in Nishapur informed us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Ali al-Bayhaqi narrated to us from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Sulami from Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-'Asmi from Abu Ishaq Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Yasin al-Harawi who said: I heard Ibrahim ibn Ishaq al-Ansari say: I heard al-Marwarrudhi, the companion of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, say: Ahmad said: When I am asked about a matter for which I know no report (khabar), I say in it: 'Al-Shafi'i says such-and-such,' because he is an imam, a scholar from Quraysh. And it was narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'A scholar from Quraysh will fill the earth with knowledge.' And it is mentioned in the report that Allah will appoint...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a biographical report about Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's high regard for Imam al-Shafi'i. It is transmitted through a chain leading to al-Marwarrudhi, a companion of Ahmad. Ahmad states that when he is asked about a legal issue for which he knows no explicit textual evidence (khabar), he relies on the opinion of al-Shafi'i, saying 'Al-Shafi'i says such-and-such.' The reason he gives is that al-Shafi'i is an imam, a scholar from Quraysh. This indicates that Ahmad considered al-Shafi'i to be a source of authority in matters of law, especially when direct scriptural evidence was lacking. Then Ahmad references a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that 'a scholar from Quraysh will fill the earth with knowledge,' implying that al-Shafi'i is that scholar. The passage ends abruptly with 'and it is mentioned in the report that Allah will appoint...' (likely referring to the continuation of the hadith or another tradition). This passage demonstrates the mutual respect among early Sunni imams and specifically elevates al-Shafi'i as a renewer of knowledge.

عالم قريش

قریش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam Ahmad always followed al-Shafi'i's opinions.
Correction: Ahmad only relied on al-Shafi'i when he had no explicit textual report on the matter, not as a general rule.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam Ahmad's reliance on al-Shafi'i for issues where he lacked direct evidence highlights the humility and mutual respect among early imams, and ties to a prophetic promise about a Qurayshi scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Hadith of the Renewer and Its Early Interpretation
Narrates the renewer hadith via two chains and identifies Umar and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wording and dual transmission of the renewer hadith, and the early scholarly identification of Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and Imam al-Shafi'i as the renewers of the first two centuries.

Core Idea
The renewer hadith promises a reviver of religion every century, with early scholars identifying Umar and Shafi'i.

This lesson presents the famous hadith about the renewer (mujaddid) as transmitted through two chains from Abu Hurayra. It also records an early application where companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and Muhammad bin Idris al-Shafi'i. Understanding this hadith and its early interpretation helps us appreciate the concept of renewal in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its two chains
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the hadith is transmitted through two separate chains, both ending with Abu Hurayra. The second chain includes an additional identification of the renewers.
The first chain is via Abu Dawud, the second via Ibn Wahb and others.
2
Identify the promise and its timing
The hadith states that Allah will raise for this community at the head of every hundred years someone who renews its religion. Note the phrase 'on the head of every hundred years' meaning at the beginning of each century.
3
Observe the early application
After the second chain, the narrator Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn reports that his companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz for the first century and al-Shafi'i for the second.
This is an early example of applying the hadith to specific historical figures.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why Umar bin Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i were chosen. Consider their contributions to Islamic scholarship and revival. Also note that the hadith does not name individuals; the identification is interpretive.
This connects to the common misunderstanding that the hadith specifies particular individuals.

Ahmad bin al-Qasim bin Ja'far bin Abd al-Wahid al-Hashimi narrated to us: Abu Ali Muhammad bin Amr al-Lu'lu'i narrated to us, Abu Dawud Sulayman bin al-Ash'ath al-Sijistani narrated to us in the book of Sunan, he said: Sulayman bin Dawud al-Mahri narrated to us, Ibn Wahb informed us, Sa'id bin Abi Ayyub informed me from Shirahil bin Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqama from Abu Hurayra, as far as I know, from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, will raise for this community at the head of every hundred years one who will renew its religion for it.' Abu Dawud said: The Shaykh Abd al-Rahman bin Shurayh al-Iskandarani narrated it, he did not inform Shirahil of it. We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il bin Ahmad al-Samarqandi, we were informed by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il bin Mas'ada al-Jurjani in Baghdad, we were informed by Abu al-Qasim Hamza bin Yusuf al-Sahmi, we were informed by Abu Ahmad Abd Allah bin Adi al-Jurjani, we were informed by al-Abbas bin Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Basri and al-Qasim bin Abd Allah bin Mahdi, they said: Humaym narrated to us, they said: Amr bin Sawad al-Sarhi narrated to us. Abu Ahmad bin Adi said: And Yahya bin Muhammad bin Yahya, the nephew of Harmala bin Yahya, narrated to us, they said: Harmala bin Yahya narrated to us. Abu Ahmad said: And Muhammad bin Harun bin Hassan and Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn narrated to us, they said: Ahmad bin Abd al-Rahman bin Wahb narrated to us, they said: Ibn Wahb narrated to us, he said: Sa'id bin Abi Ayyub narrated to me from Shirahil bin Yazid al-Ma'afiri from Abu 'Alqama from Abu Hurayra, as far as I know, from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'Indeed Allah raises for this community at the head of every hundred years one who renews its religion for it.' Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn said: I heard our companions saying: In the first century it was Umar bin Abd al-Aziz, and in the second century it was Muhammad bin Idris al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a dual transmission of the famous hadith about the renewer (mujaddid). It presents two chains: one via Abu Dawud and another via Ibn Wahb, both from Abu Hurayra with the same wording. After the second chain, the narrator Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Husayn reports that his companions identified the renewers of the first two centuries: Umar bin Abd al-Aziz for the first century and Imam al-Shafi'i for the second. This establishes an early precedent for applying the hadith to specific scholars, linking the concept of renewal to key figures in Islamic history.

Misconception: The hadith names specific individuals as renewers for each century.
Correction: The hadith is a generic promise that Allah will raise a renewer; the identification of Umar and Shafi'i is an interpretive application by early scholars, not a direct statement of the hadith.

Ahmad ibn Hanbal on al-Shafi'i and the Renewer
Ahmad ibn Hanbal praises al-Shafi'i and identifies him as the second renewer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahmad ibn Hanbal viewed al-Shafi'i as an authoritative source and connected him to the prophetic tradition of religious renewal.

Core Idea
Ahmad ibn Hanbal relied on al-Shafi'i as a Quraysh scholar and renewer.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work preserves a remarkable statement from Ahmad ibn Hanbal showing his deep respect for al-Shafi'i. Ahmad explains that when he lacks direct textual evidence, he turns to al-Shafi'i's opinion because of his lineage and knowledge. He then links al-Shafi'i to the famous hadith about a renewer every century, identifying him as the renewer of the second Islamic century. This lesson explores the significance of these claims and what they reveal about early scholarly relationships.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the key statements from Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
The isnad shows this information was transmitted through reliable scholars like al-Bayhaqi.
2
Understand Ahmad's practice
Ahmad says he quotes al-Shafi'i when he doesn't know a report. Ask: Why does he choose al-Shafi'i specifically? What does this tell us about Ahmad's methodology?
Ahmad does not follow al-Shafi'i blindly; he acknowledges his authority in certain cases.
3
Connect to the renewer tradition
Ahmad cites the hadith about a renewer every hundred years and explicitly names Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i as the first two renewers. Reflect on the implications for al-Shafi'i's status.
This shows that early scholars saw renewal as a continuous process.
4
Note the supplication for al-Shafi'i
The narrator Abu Abd Allah says he has been praying for al-Shafi'i in his prayers for forty years. Consider what this demonstrates about personal devotion and respect.
This indicates that al-Shafi'i was held in high esteem even by later scholars.

We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad bin Isma'il bin Muhammad bin al-Husayn al-Farisi in Nishapur: Abu Bakr Ahmad bin al-Husayn bin Ali al-Bayhaqi informed us: Abu Abd al-Rahman Muhammad bin al-Husayn al-Sulami informed us: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad bin al-Abbas al-Asami narrated to us: Abu Ishaq Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Yasin al-Harawi narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibrahim bin Ishaq al-Ansari say: I heard al-Marwadhi, the companion of Ahmad bin Hanbal, say: Ahmad said: 'If I am asked about a matter for which I know no report, I say in it: al-Shafi'i says, because he is an imam from Quraysh.' The passage demonstrates the high esteem later scholars held for al-Shafi'i and connects him to the renewal tradition.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Three Revivers of Religion: Ahmad, Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aim
Report of al-Sa'luki crediting three scholars with reviving religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the report crediting three scholars—Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi—with reviving Islam after it had largely disappeared.

Core Idea
Allah revived religion through three scholars: Ahmad, Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aim.

This lesson presents a concise yet powerful report from the renowned scholar Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki (with a note of narrator uncertainty). It identifies three figures who, according to al-Sa'luki, were instruments of Allah in restoring the religion after a period of decline. As you read, note the chain of transmission and the precise wording, which highlights the collaborative role of these scholars in reviving Islamic knowledge and practice.

Guided Path
1
Examine the transmission chain
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the chain from the author through al-Qumisi, al-Sahlaki, and al-Razjahi, with the narrator's uncertainty about whether the speaker was al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili. This shows the care in preserving reports.
The uncertainty is captured by the phrase 'أو الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر الإسمعيلي' and 'والشك مني'.
2
Identify the three scholars named
Find the names: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi. Reflect on their fields: hadith/fiqh, theology, and spirituality.
Each scholar contributed uniquely to the revival of Sunnism.
3
Understand the meaning of 'reviving religion'
The phrase 'بعد ما ذهب' suggests a period when the religion had largely disappeared. The revival means restoring its teachings and practices.
This is not about physical revival but renewal of knowledge and adherence.
4
Consider the narrator's doubt
The transmitter is unsure whether the saying came from al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili. This does not affect the content but reminds us of the human element in transmission.
Such doubts are common in hadith and historical reports.

اخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر أحمد بن الحسين القومسى بها انا جدى لأمى أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد السهلكي قال حكى الفقيه الصالح الثقة أبو عمرو یعنی محمد بن عبدالله الأديب الرزجاهى قال سمعت الاستاذ الامام ابا سهل الصعلوكي ام الشيخ الامام ابا بكر الاسمعيلى ذكر واحدا والشك منى يقول : اعاد الله تعالى هذا الدين بعد ماذهب يعنى اكثره بأحمد بن حنبل وابي الحسن الأشعري وابي نعيم الاسترابادى
We were informed by al-Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Ahmad bin al-Husayn al-Qumisi there: my maternal grandfather Abu al-Fadl Muhammad bin Ali bin Ahmad al-Sahlaki informed us, he said: The righteous and trustworthy jurist Abu Amr, meaning Muhammad bin Abd Allah al-Adib al-Razjahi, related: I heard the teacher and imam Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki, or the shaykh and imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili? — he mentioned one, and I am uncertain — say: 'Allah, Exalted, restored this religion after it had gone, meaning most of it, through Ahmad bin Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi.'
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a report from al-Sa'luki (with a note of uncertainty from the transmitter about whether it was al-Sa'luki or al-Isma'ili) stating that Allah revived the religion after it had largely disappeared through three scholars: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Istirabadi. This presents a broader view of renewal involving multiple figures across different fields: hadith and fiqh (Ahmad), theology and defense of Sunnism (Ash'ari), and perhaps hadith or Sufism (Abu Nu'aim). The phrasing 'after it had gone' suggests a period of decline followed by revival through these scholars' efforts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If Allah revives religion through scholars, what are you doing to ensure you are not part of a generation that lets the religion 'go' again? What personal accountability do you feel for the preservation of true Islam?

Identifying the Renewers: Al-Sulami's List and Ibn Asakir's Corrections
Lists renewers for five centuries, author adds al-Ghazali and prefers Ash'ari and Baqillani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical scholars like Ibn Asakir evaluated competing claims of who the renewer (mujaddid) was for each century, prioritizing those who defended the Sunnah and had widespread scholarly impact.

Core Idea
Renewers of Islam are identified by their role in defending the Sunnah, not merely by legal expertise.

This passage presents a fascinating scholarly debate about exactly which figures should be counted as the renewers (mujaddids) for the first five centuries of Islam. You will read a report from Abu al-Hasan al-Sulami listing his candidates, then see how the author (Ibn Asakir) interjects his own corrections and preferences. Through this, you'll gain insight into the criteria that classical scholars used to evaluate a scholar's impact on the renewal of religion.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Sulami's list of renewers
Read the Arabic passage noting the five centuries and the names given by al-Sulami: Umar, al-Shafi'i, al-Ash'ari, al-Baqillani, and al-Mustarshid.
This list is the starting point for the debate.
2
Identify the author's correction
Notice where the author says 'But in my opinion' and replaces al-Mustarshid with al-Ghazali for the fifth century, supporting his choice with Ghazali's virtues.
The author prioritizes a scholar's widespread fame and scholarly output.
3
Analyze the alternative views
Read the part where others propose Ibn Surayj for the third century and al-Sa'luki for the fourth, and note how the author rebuts these.
The author judges based on the scholar's role in refuting innovators.
4
Understand the criteria
Reflect on why the author considers al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani more deserving: their active defense of the Sunnah against the Mu'tazila and other groups.
Impact on preserving correct belief is key.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسمعت الشيخ الامام ابا الحسن علی بن المسلم بن محمد بن على بن الفتح بن على السلمى على كرسيه بجامع دمشق يقول وذكر حديث ابي علقمة هذا فقال : كان على رأس المائة الأولى عمر بن عبد العزيز وكان على رأس المائة الثانية محمد بن ادريس الشافعي وكان على رأس المائة الثالثة الأشعرى وكان على رأس المائة الرابعة ابن الباقلاني وكان على رأس المائة الخامسة امير المؤمنين المسترشد بالله، وعندى ان الذي كان على رأس الخمس مائة الأمام أبو ماجد محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن محمد الغزالي الطوسي الفقيه، لأنه كان عالما عاملا فقيها فاضلا أصوليا كاملا مصنفا عاقلا، انتشر ذكره بالعلم في الآفاق وبرز على من عاصره بخراسان والشام والعراق، وذكر غير الفقيه ابى الحسن ان ابا العباس أحمد ابن عمر بن سريج الفقيه هو الذى كان على رأس الثلثمائة وان ابا الطيب سهل بن محمد بن سليمان الصعلوكي النيسابوري هو الذي كان على . رأس الاربعمائة، وقول من قال انه أبو الحسن الأشعری اصوب لأن قيامه بنصرة السنة إلى تجديد الدين أقرب فهو الذي انتدب للرد على المعتزلة وسائر اصناف المبتدعة المضللة وحالته فى ذلك مشتهرة وكتبه في الرد عليهم منتشرة، فأما أبو العباس بن سريج فكان فقيها مضطلعا بعلم اصول الفقه وفروعه نبيها وقول من قال ان القاضى ابا بكر محمد بن الطيب الباقلاني هو الذى كان على رأس الاربعمائة اولى من القول الثاني لأنه اشهر من أبي الطيب الصعلوكى مكانا وأعلى فى رتب القوم شانا وذكره اكبر من
And I heard the shaykh and imam Abu al-Hasan Ali bin al-Muslim bin Muhammad bin Ali bin al-Fath bin Ali al-Sulami on his pulpit in the Umayyad Mosque of Damascus, saying — and he mentioned this hadith of Abu 'Alqama — and he said: 'At the head of the first century was Umar bin Abd al-Aziz; at the head of the second century was Muhammad bin Idris al-Shafi'i; at the head of the third century was al-Ash'ari; at the head of the fourth century was Ibn al-Baqillani; at the head of the fifth century was the Commander of the Faithful al-Mustarshid bi-Allah.' But in my opinion, the one at the head of five hundred was the imam Abu Majid Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Muhammad al-Ghazali al-Tusi the jurist, because he was a scholar, a practitioner, a jurist, virtuous, a perfect usuli, a prolific author, intelligent; his fame for knowledge spread to the horizons, and he excelled those of his time in Khurasan, Syria, and Iraq. And someone other than the jurist Abu al-Hasan mentioned that Abu al-Abbas Ahmad bin Umar bin Surayj the jurist was the one at the head of three hundred, and that Abu al-Tayyib Sahl bin Muhammad bin Sulayman al-Sa'luki al-Naysaburi was the one at the head of four hundred. But the statement of those who say that it was Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is more correct, because his undertaking to support the Sunnah is closer to the renewal of religion; he is the one who undertook to refute the Mu'tazila and all other misguiding innovators, and his state in that is well-known, and his books refuting them are widespread. As for Abu al-Abbas bin Surayj, he was a jurist capable in the science of usul al-fiqh and its branches, insightful. And the statement of those who say that the judge Abu Bakr Muhammad bin al-Tayyib al-Baqillani was the one at the head of four hundred is more worthy than the second statement, because he is more famous than Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luki in stature and higher in rank among the people, and his mention is greater than... [text cut off]
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage, from page 54, is a report of a sermon by Abu al-Hasan al-Sulami identifying renewers for the first five centuries: Umar, Shafi'i, Ash'ari, Baqillani, and Caliph al-Mustarshid. The author (likely Ibn Asakir) then interjects his own opinion, correcting the fifth to al-Ghazali, praising his scholarship, practice, and fame. The passage then discusses alternative views: some say Ibn Surayj for the third century and al-Sa'luki for the fourth. The author evaluates these, preferring al-Ash'ari for the third because of his role in defending the Sunnah against the Mu'tazila and other innovators, supported by his well-known works. For the fourth, he prefers al-Baqillani over al-Sa'luki due to his greater stature and fame. The text is cut off, but the argument prioritizes scholars who most directly and demonstrably defended and renewed the Sunnah.

المسترشد بالله
الغزالي
ابن سريج
الصعلوكي
أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The list of renewers for each century is fixed and universally agreed upon.
Correction: This passage shows that the identification of renewers involves scholarly debate and personal ijtihad; different scholars have proposed different names based on criteria like defense of the Sunnah and impact.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir demonstrates that identifying a renewer involves weighing a scholar's contributions to defending the Sunnah and their impact across regions, rather than relying solely on a fixed list.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you spoke up to defend a belief of the Sunnah in a conversation where it was being criticized or mocked? If you cannot recall such a moment, what does that say about your commitment to the truth that the renewers lived and died for? Will you commit to at least one such act this week?
?
Imagine you are evaluated by the same measure Ibn Asakir used for the renewers: your contribution to the defense and spread of authentic Islam. Not your titles or reputation, but your actual impact. Would the verdict be 'more correct' or 'less worthy'? What is the first change you must make today?
?
Al-Ghazali excelled in many fields: fiqh, usul, kalam, tazkiya. You know your own strengths and weaknesses. Which area of Islamic knowledge or practice are you neglecting? Write down one concrete step to develop it, and tell a friend who will hold you accountable by the end of this week.

The Hadith of the Renewer and the First Two Centuries
Hadith of the renewer and identification of first two renewers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about a renewer at the head of every century and the identification of the first two renewers by Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Core Idea
Every century, Allah sends a renewer of religion.

This lesson introduces a well-known hadith about a renewer (mujaddid) appearing at the start of each century to revive religious knowledge. The great imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal transmits this hadith and then gives his own opinion on who the renewers were for the first two centuries: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Begin by reading the Arabic hadith and its translation. Notice that the Prophet (peace be upon him) is reported to have promised a renewer for every century.
The chain of narration goes back to Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
2
Identify the first two renewers
Ahmad ibn Hanbal identifies Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz for the first century and al-Shafi'i for the second. Why were these scholars chosen? Consider their roles in reviving the Sunnah and knowledge.
Umar is known for his just caliphate, al-Shafi'i for systematizing Islamic jurisprudence.
3
Reflect on the supplication for al-Shafi'i
Ahmad ibn Hanbal added that he had been supplicating for al-Shafi'i for forty years in his prayers. This shows the deep respect and gratitude he had for al-Shafi'i’s contribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في رأس كل مائة سنة رجلا يعلم الناس دينهم وروى أحمد بن حنبل ذلك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال أحمد بن حنبل فكان في المائة الأولى عمر بن عبدالعزيز وفي المائة الثانية الشافعي قال أبو عـبـد الله وانا ادعـو للشافعي منذ أربعين سنة في صلاتي اخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر أحمد بن الحسين القومسى بها انا جدى لأمى أبو الفضل محمد بن على بن أحمد السهلكي قال حكى الفقيه الصالح الثقة أبو عمرو یعنی محمد بن عبدالله الأديب الرزجاهى قال سمعت الاستاذ الامام ابا سهل الصعلوكي ام الشيخ الامام ابا بكر الاسمعيلى ذكر واحدا والشك منى يقول : اعاد الله تعالى هذا الدين بعد ماذهب يعنى اكثره بأحمد بن حنبل وابي الحسن الأشعري وابي نعيم الاسترابادى وسمعت الشيخ الامام ابا الحسن علی بن المسلم بن محمد بن على بن الفتح بن على السلمى على كرسيه بجامع دمشق يقول وذكر حديث ابي علقمة هذا فقال : كان على رأس المائة الأولى عمر بن عبد العزيز وكان على رأس المائة الثانية محمد بن ادريس الشافعي وكان على رأس المائة الثالثة الأشعرى وكان على رأس المائة الرابعة ابن الباقلاني وكان على رأس المائة الخامسة امير المؤمنين المسترشد بالله، وعندى ان الذي كان على رأس الخمس مائة الأمام أبو ماجد محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن محمد الغزالي الطوسي الفقيه، لأنه كان عالما عاملا فقيها فاضلا أصوليا كاملا مصنفا عاقلا، انتشر ذكره بالعلم في الآفاق وبرز على من عاصره بخراسان والشام والعراق
At the head of every hundred years, a man who teaches the people their religion. Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated that from the Prophet, peace be upon him. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: In the first century, it was Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz; in the second century, al-Shafi'i. Abu Abd Allah said: I have been supplicating for al-Shafi'i in my prayer for forty years. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Qumasi informed us by it: my maternal grandfather Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sahlaki narrated to us: the righteous trustworthy jurist Abu Amr – meaning Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Adib al-Razjahi – said: I heard the master Imam Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki, or Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, mention one – and the doubt is from me – saying: Allah Almighty restored this religion after it had gone, meaning most of it, through Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. And I heard the Shaykh al-Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Muslim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Fath ibn Ali al-Sulami on his chair in the Damascus Mosque saying – and he mentioned the hadith of Abu 'Alqama – and said: At the head of the first century was Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz; at the head of the second century was Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i; at the head of the third century was al-Ash'ari; at the head of the fourth century was Ibn al-Baqillani; at the head of the fifth century was the Commander of the Faithful al-Mustarshid bi-Allah. And in my view, the one who was at the head of five hundred years is the Imam Abu Majid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali al-Tusi al-Faqih, because he was a scholar, a practitioner, a jurist, a virtuous man, a perfect usuli, a prolific author, an intelligent man; his fame spread through knowledge in the horizons, and he excelled over his contemporaries in Khurasan, Syria, and Iraq.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents a tradition (hadith) about a renewer (mujaddid) appearing at the head of every century to teach religion. The author, Ibn Asakir, first cites the narration from Ahmad ibn Hanbal attributing this to the Prophet. Ahmad then identifies Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz for the first century and al-Shafi'i for the second. The author adds a personal note from Abu Abd Allah (likely Ahmad ibn Hanbal himself) that he has been supplicating for al-Shafi'i in prayer for forty years. Then through a chain of transmission, Ibn Asakir reports a statement from Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki or Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili (with doubt from the narrator) that Allah restored the religion through three figures: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. Following this, Ibn Asakir transmits from al-Sulami a different list: Umar (1st), al-Shafi'i (2nd), al-Ash'ari (3rd), Ibn al-Baqillani (4th), and al-Mustarshid bi-Allah (5th). Finally, the author gives his own opinion: the one at the head of 500 years (i.e., the sixth century) is Imam al-Ghazali, listing his virtues and widespread reputation. This shows the author's adherence to the mujaddid tradition and his preference for al-Ghazali.

Key Terms
رأس كل مائة سنة
مجدّد
المائة الأولى
المائة الثانية
عمر بن عبدالعزيز
الشافعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith specifies that the renewer must be a single person per century universally agreed upon.
Correction: The hadith mentions a renewer but does not name them; the identification is based on the ijtihad of scholars like Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The hadith establishes the concept of a renewer for every century, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal identifies Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and al-Shafi'i as the first two.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Have you personally benefited from his teaching, or are you neglecting the opportunity? Commit today to seeking knowledge from a qualified teacher this week.
?
Ahmad ibn Hanbal made dua for al-Shafi'i for forty years. Think of the scholars who have guided you—do you ever make dua for them? If not, start now. Write down the name of one scholar you can pray for regularly.
?
If a renewer appears to revive religion, then each of us has a responsibility to receive that renewal. What is one area of your religious practice that has become stagnant or neglected? How will you respond to the call of renewal before the next century begins? Take one concrete action today.

The Restoration of Religion Through Three Scholars
Statement that Allah restored religion through three scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how some early scholars held that Allah restored the religion through three key figures: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini.

Core Idea
Allah restored religion through three: Ahmad, Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym.

This lesson presents a tradition transmitted by Ibn Asakir from earlier authorities. It states that after most of the religion had disappeared, Allah revived it through three individuals: the great hadith master Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the theologian Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and the Shafi'i scholar Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. This highlights the importance of these figures in preserving Islamic orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the transmission chain
Notice the chain of narrators leading back to Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki or Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. This gives the statement credibility through a scholarly line.
The doubt about the exact narrator shows careful transmission.
2
Identify the three restorers
The statement names Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. Why are these three linked together? They represent hadith, theology, and jurisprudence respectively.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'restoration'
The phrase 'after it had gone, meaning most of it' suggests a period of decline. These scholars revived essential aspects of the religion through their works and teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

At the head of every hundred years, a man who teaches the people their religion. Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated that from the Prophet, peace be upon him. Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: In the first century, it was Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz; in the second century, al-Shafi'i. Abu Abd Allah said: I have been supplicating for al-Shafi'i in my prayer for forty years. Al-Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Qumasi informed us by it: my maternal grandfather Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Ahmad al-Sahlaki narrated to us: the righteous trustworthy jurist Abu Amr – meaning Muhammad ibn Abd Allah al-Adib al-Razjahi – said: I heard the master Imam Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki, or Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, mention one – and the doubt is from me – saying: Allah Almighty restored this religion after it had gone, meaning most of it, through Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. And I heard the Shaykh al-Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Muslim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Fath ibn Ali al-Sulami on his chair in the Damascus Mosque saying – and he mentioned the hadith of Abu 'Alqama – and said: At the head of the first century was Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz; at the head of the second century was Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i; at the head of the third century was al-Ash'ari; at the head of the fourth century was Ibn al-Baqillani; at the head of the fifth century was the Commander of the Faithful al-Mustarshid bi-Allah. And in my view, the one who was at the head of five hundred years is the Imam Abu Majid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali al-Tusi al-Faqih, because he was a scholar, a practitioner, a jurist, a virtuous man, a perfect usuli, a prolific author, an intelligent man; his fame spread through knowledge in the horizons, and he excelled over his contemporaries in Khurasan, Syria, and Iraq.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents a tradition (hadith) about a renewer (mujaddid) appearing at the head of every century to teach religion. The author, Ibn Asakir, first cites the narration from Ahmad ibn Hanbal attributing this to the Prophet. Ahmad then identifies Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz for the first century and al-Shafi'i for the second. The author adds a personal note from Abu Abd Allah (likely Ahmad ibn Hanbal himself) that he has been supplicating for al-Shafi'i in prayer for forty years. Then through a chain of transmission, Ibn Asakir reports a statement from Abu Sahl al-Sa'luki or Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili (with doubt from the narrator) that Allah restored the religion through three figures: Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini. Following this, Ibn Asakir transmits from al-Sulami a different list: Umar (1st), al-Shafi'i (2nd), al-Ash'ari (3rd), Ibn al-Baqillani (4th), and al-Mustarshid bi-Allah (5th). Finally, the author gives his own opinion: the one at the head of 500 years (i.e., the sixth century) is Imam al-Ghazali, listing his virtues and widespread reputation. This shows the author's adherence to the mujaddid tradition and his preference for al-Ghazali.

Key Terms
أحمد بن حنبل
أبو الحسن الأشعري
أبو نعيم الاسترابادى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only one person can restore the religion at a time.
Correction: The statement shows that multiple scholars can play a role, each in a different field.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three scholars through whom Allah restored the religion according to this passage?
A) Ahmad ibn Hanbal
B) Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari
C) Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini
D) Al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Allah revived the religion through the combined efforts of Ahmad ibn Hanbal (hadith), al-Ash'ari (theology), and Abu Nu'aym (jurisprudence).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson tells you that Allah restored the religion through three scholars representing hadith, theology, and jurisprudence. Which of these three areas do you find yourself neglecting most in your daily practice? What is one concrete action you will take this week to strengthen that area?
?
If the religion was restored through the efforts of these scholars, are you contributing to its preservation in your time? Think of one thing you do – or fail to do – that either strengthens or weakens the religion around you. What will you change starting today?
?
The chain of narrators in this passage includes a doubt about who said the statement. Does your own transmission of Islamic knowledge come with the same level of accuracy and care? How often do you check your sources before passing on religious information? Commit to one change in how you verify knowledge.

The Ash'ari Chain of Renewers and al-Ghazali
List of renewers up to fifth century and Ibn Asakir's choice of al-Ghazali for the sixth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the list of renewers provided by al-Sulami (including al-Ash'ari, al-Baqillani, and al-Mustarshid) and Ibn Asakir's opinion that al-Ghazali was the renewer at the head of the sixth century.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali is the renewer of the sixth century in Ibn Asakir's view.

This lesson presents another list of renewers, transmitted by al-Sulami, which includes al-Ash'ari, al-Baqillani, and the Abbasid caliph al-Mustarshid for the first five centuries. Following that, Ibn Asakir gives his own considered opinion: the renewer at the head of the sixth century (500 AH) is Imam Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, whom he praises with multiple attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the list from al-Sulami
Al-Sulami gives a sequence: Umar, al-Shafi'i, al-Ash'ari, al-Baqillani, and al-Mustarshid. Notice how it shifts from caliphs to scholars and back to a caliph.
2
Compare with the earlier lists
Compare this list with the one from Ahmad ibn Hanbal. What is similar? What is different? Al-Ash'ari and al-Baqillani are new additions.
This list extends to the fifth century.
3
Examine Ibn Asakir's opinion on al-Ghazali
Ibn Asakir asserts that al-Ghazali is the renewer at 500 AH. He lists his virtues: scholar, practitioner, jurist, virtuous, usuli, author, intelligent. This shows the high esteem in which al-Ghazali was held.
Al-Ghazali died in 505 AH, so this fits chronologically.

Biography of Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini
Ibn Asakir transmits biographical data on Abu Nu'aym via a chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical details of Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini as transmitted by Ibn Asakir, including his scholarly status and death date.

Core Idea
Chains of transmission preserve the trustworthiness of historical reports.

Ibn Asakir begins his biographical entry on Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini by citing a chain of narrators leading to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. This chain establishes the authority of the information about Abu Nu'aym's life and scholarship. Let's explore what is said about him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the chain of narrators at the beginning.
The chain includes al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
2
Identify Abu Nu'aym's identity
Find the name and lineage: Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani al-Faqih. Note his title 'al-Isfarayini' refers to his origin.
3
Note the qualities attributed
Al-Khatib describes him as an Imam, Hafiz, with truthfulness, piety, precision, and vigilance. He traveled widely and wrote in many regions.
4
Record his death date
He died around 320 AH. The author adds that he supported the Sunnah in Jurjan.
The date is approximate ('around').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاما أبو نعيم الاستراباذي فهو عبدالملك الجرجاني الفقيه، قال لنا أبو الحسين على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن زريق الشيباني ببغداد، قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب إنه كان أحد أئمة المسلمين ومن الحفاظ في الشرائع والدين مع الحفاظ فى الشرائع والدين مع صدق وتورع وضبط وتيقظ، سافر الكثير وكتب بالعراق والحجاز والشام ومصر ومات حدود سنة عشرين وثلثمائة قلت وكان ينصر السنة بجرجان فاما عمر بن عبد العزيز بن مروان بن الحكم بن ابی العاص ابن زمـيـة بن عبد شمس وكانت وفاته كما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو غالب أحمد بن الحسن بن أحمد بن البناء ببغداد قال انا أبو الحسين محمد بن أحمد بن محمد ابن علی بن الأبنوسى انا أبو القسم عبد الله بن عثمان بن يحيى بن خبيق الدقاق، انا أبو محمد اسمعیل بن علی بن اسماعيل الخطبى قال اخبرنی محمد بن موسى بن حماد البربرى عن محمد بن ابى السرى ان عمر بن عبدالعزيز توفى لأربع ليال يعني من رجب سنة احدى ومائة وهو ابن تسع وثلاثين سنة ونصف، قال ابن ابى السرى قال العمرى توفى يوم الجمعة لخمس ليال بقين من رجب وقبره بدير سمعان وكانت ولايته سنتين وخمسة أشهر وخمسة أيام، وأما الشافعى فكانت وفاته فيما اخبرنا الشيخ الفقيه أبو الحسن على بن المسلم السلمى انا أبو نصر الحسين بن محمد بن
As for Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini, he is Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani al-Faqih. Abu al-Husayn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Zurayq al-Shaybani in Baghdad said to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: He was one of the Imams of the Muslims and among the memorizers of the laws and religion, with truthfulness, piety, precision, and vigilance. He traveled extensively and wrote in Iraq, Hijaz, Syria, and Egypt, and he died around the year 320. I say: He was supporting the Sunnah in Jurjan. As for Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Marwan ibn al-Hakam ibn Abi al-As ibn Umayya ibn Abd Shams, his death was as informed by Shaykh Abu Ghalib Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Banna in Baghdad: Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Abnusi narrated to us: Abu al-Qasim Abd Allah ibn Uthman ibn Yahya ibn Khubayq al-Daqqaq narrated to us: Abu Muhammad Isma'il ibn Ali ibn Isma'il al-Khatabi narrated to us: Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Hammad al-Barbari informed me from Muhammad ibn Abi al-Sari: that Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz died on the fourth night (meaning of Rajab) in the year 101, and he was 39 and a half years old. Ibn Abi al-Sari said: Al-Umari said: He died on Friday, five nights remaining of Rajab, and his grave is in Dayr Sim'an, and his reign was two years, five months, and five days. As for al-Shafi'i, his death was as informed by the Shaykh al-Faqih Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Muslim al-Sulami: Abu Nasr al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides biographical summaries of three important figures. First, Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini: the author identifies him as Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani al-Faqih, citing al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's praise that he was an Imam and a Hafiz in religious sciences, known for truthfulness and precision. He traveled widely and died around 320 AH. The author adds that he supported the Sunnah in Jurjan. Second, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: the author details his lineage and then gives a precise account of his death through a chain of narration. He died in Rajab 101 AH, at age 39.5, after a reign of 2 years, 5 months, and 5 days, and was buried in Dayr Sim'an. Third, al-Shafi'i: the passage begins his death notice but is cut off at page end. The chain includes Abu al-Hasan al-Sulami narrating from Abu Nasr al-Husayn. This shows Ibn Asakir's method of transmitting biographical data with full chains.

Key Terms
أبو نعيم الاستراباذي
الخطيب البغدادي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The chains of narration are just a formality and not essential for historical trust.
Correction: Chains are crucial for verifying the authenticity and transmission of reports; they connect the report back to reliable authorities.

Checkpoint

A) 310 AH
B) 320 AH

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Are your comforts hindering your pursuit of truth? Commit to one concrete change in your daily routine to prioritize Islamic knowledge, even if it costs you convenience.
?
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi testified that Abu Nu'aym had 'truthfulness, piety, precision, and vigilance.' Which of these qualities are you most lacking in your own learning and practice? Be honest. Write down a specific action you can take this week to strengthen that quality, and ask someone to hold you accountable.
?
The chain of narrators in this passage is what makes the report reliable. Think about the sources of your own religious knowledge: do you even know who transmitted them? How can you accept a teaching without verifying its chain? Starting today, resolve to trace every important religious claim back to its source, and if you cannot, humbly admit you do not know.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

Biography of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz
Ibn Asakir records the death details of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz with a full chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the precise death date, age, reign length, and burial place of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz as recorded by Ibn Asakir through a chain of narration.

Core Idea
Every detail of a pious caliph's life is preserved through trustworthy chains.

Ibn Asakir provides a detailed account of the death of the Umayyad caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Through a chain of narrators, he gives the exact date, his age, and the length of his caliphate. This precision reflects the care historians take in preserving important events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the full lineage
Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Marwan ibn al-Hakam etc. This establishes his Umayyad genealogy.
2
Trace the chain of narration
Note the narrators: from Ibn al-Banna to al-Khatabi to Muhammad ibn Abi al-Sari. The chain is long, indicating careful transmission.
The final authority is Muhammad ibn Abi al-Sari.
3
Extract the key numerical details
Death: Rajab 101 AH, age 39.5, reign 2 years 5 months 5 days. Burial: Dayr Sim'an.
Two slightly different reports are given for the exact day.
4
Reflect on the importance of these details
Such precision allows historians to cross-check events. It also honors the legacy of a caliph known for justice.

As for Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini, he is Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani al-Faqih. Abu al-Husayn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Zurayq al-Shaybani in Baghdad said to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: He was one of the Imams of the Muslims and among the memorizers of the laws and religion, with truthfulness, piety, precision, and vigilance. He traveled extensively and wrote in Iraq, Hijaz, Syria, and Egypt, and he died around the year 320. I say: He was supporting the Sunnah in Jurjan. As for Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Marwan ibn al-Hakam ibn Abi al-As ibn Umayya ibn Abd Shams, his death was as informed by Shaykh Abu Ghalib Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Banna in Baghdad: Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Abnusi narrated to us: Abu al-Qasim Abd Allah ibn Uthman ibn Yahya ibn Khubayq al-Daqqaq narrated to us: Abu Muhammad Isma'il ibn Ali ibn Isma'il al-Khatabi narrated to us: Muhammad ibn Musa ibn Hammad al-Barbari informed me from Muhammad ibn Abi al-Sari: that Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz died on the fourth night (meaning of Rajab) in the year 101, and he was 39 and a half years old. Ibn Abi al-Sari said: Al-Umari said: He died on Friday, five nights remaining of Rajab, and his grave is in Dayr Sim'an, and his reign was two years, five months, and five days. As for al-Shafi'i, his death was as informed by the Shaykh al-Faqih Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn al-Muslim al-Sulami: Abu Nasr al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides biographical summaries of three important figures. First, Abu Nu'aym al-Isfarayini: the author identifies him as Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani al-Faqih, citing al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's praise that he was an Imam and a Hafiz in religious sciences, known for truthfulness and precision. He traveled widely and died around 320 AH. The author adds that he supported the Sunnah in Jurjan. Second, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: the author details his lineage and then gives a precise account of his death through a chain of narration. He died in Rajab 101 AH, at age 39.5, after a reign of 2 years, 5 months, and 5 days, and was buried in Dayr Sim'an. Third, al-Shafi'i: the passage begins his death notice but is cut off at page end. The chain includes Abu al-Hasan al-Sulami narrating from Abu Nasr al-Husayn. This shows Ibn Asakir's method of transmitting biographical data with full chains.

Key Terms
عمر بن عبد العزيز
دير سمعان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The precise numbers are likely later fabrications.
Correction: The detailed numbers are transmitted via chains to contemporaries, showing careful record-keeping.

Checkpoint

B) 101 AH
C) 102 AH
D) 99 AH

Key Takeaway
The death and reign of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz are recorded with exact dates through a reliable chain of narration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The chain of narrators took great care to transmit this information accurately. How carefully do you transmit knowledge about Islam to others? Do you check your sources, or do you repeat things without verification?
?
Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz's reign was only two years, five months, and five days, yet it left a lasting legacy. If your life were summarized by a single period of responsibility, what would that summary say? And will you be content with it on the Day of Judgment?

A Family's Defense of Ash'arism in Nishapur
Ibn Asakir describes the role of Abu at-Tayyib's family in spreading Ash'arism against innovators in Nishapur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the family of Abu at-Tayyib actively propagated Ash'arism in Nishapur and refuted accusations, while defending tawhid against three innovating sects.

Core Idea
A single family championed Ash'arism against three sects: Mu'tazila, Rafida, Karramiyya.

Ibn Asakir presents a biographical vignette that demonstrates Ash'arism was not merely a theoretical school but a living tradition defended by successive generations. This passage highlights the active struggle of the family of Abu at-Tayyib in Nishapur, showing how they manifested the Ash'ari school and combated innovation. Read on to see how their legacy is used to refute false accusations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups of innovators
Read the Arabic carefully to find the three sects mentioned: al-Mu'tazila, al-Rafida, al-Karramiyya. Notice how the family fought against all of them.
These are three distinct groups that opposed Ash'arism.
2
Notice the multigenerational commitment
The passage mentions Abu at-Tayyib, his father Abu Sahl, and his son (grandson) – three generations consistently defending Ash'arism.
3
Understand the refutation of accusation
The passage connects their well-known defense of tawhid and tanzih to disprove a false accusation by Abu Ali al-Ahwazi.
This shows how scholarship and character refute calumny.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أكثر من محمد بن [بن؟] عدی ان ينكر وقدره أظهر من ان يستر وتصانيفه اشهر من ان تشهر وتواليفه ان تذكر، فاما أبو الطيب رحمه الله فانما اشتهر ذكره ببلده وكانت رياسة اصحاب الشافعي له بنيسابور ولوالده ولولده وكان ابوه أبو سهل محمد بن سليمان رحمه الله ذا محل خطير، وذكره فيما بين أهل العلم خراسان كبير لم يزل هو وولده وولد ولده يظهرون مذهب الأشعرية ويجاهدون اهل البدع بنيسابور من المعتزلة والرافضة والكرامية، وما تقدم من قوله في مدح الأشعرى مما رواه عنه أبو عمرو الرزجاهي يدل على كذب ابي على الاهوازي فيما حكى عنه اذ رماه باحدى الدواهي مع ما اشتهر عنه بخراسان من الذب عن أهل التوحيد وتنزيه الرب عز وجل عن التشبيه والتحديد مقتديا بالأشعرى وسالكا طريقه مقتفيا في علم الأصول نهجه وتحقيقه.
More than Muhammad ibn [ibn?] Adi can deny, and his rank is too apparent to be concealed, and his books are more famous than to be renowned, and his compilations are mentioned. As for Abu at-Tayyib, may God have mercy on him, his fame was only in his town, and the leadership of the Shafi'i scholars in Nishapur belonged to him, his father, and his son. His father Abu Sahl Muhammad ibn Sulayman, may God have mercy on him, was of high standing. His mention among the people of knowledge in Khorasan was great. He, his son, and his grandson never ceased to manifest the Ash'ari school and to struggle against the people of innovation in Nishapur from the Mu'tazila, Rafida, and Karramiyya. What preceded of his words in praise of al-Ash'ari, narrated from him by Abu Amr al-Razjahi, indicates the falsehood of Abu Ali al-Ahwazi in what he reported about him, when he accused him of one of the calamities, besides what is well-known about him in Khorasan of defending the people of tawhid and exalting the Lord, Mighty and Majestic, from anthropomorphism and limitation, following al-Ash'ari, traversing his path, and following his method and verification in the science of principles.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice about a family of scholars in Nishapur who championed the Ash'ari school. The author begins by praising someone (perhaps a scholar named Muhammad ibn Adi) whose works are too famous to need mention. Then he focuses on Abu at-Tayyib, a Shafi'i leader whose family inherited the leadership of the Shafi'is in Nishapur. He notes that Abu at-Tayyib's father, Abu Sahl, was highly respected. The family actively manifested the Ash'ari madhhab and struggled against innovators: the Mu'tazila, Rafida (Shi'a), and Karramiyya. The author then refers to a previous statement praising al-Ash'ari, transmitted by Abu Amr al-Razjahi, which disproves a false accusation by Abu Ali al-Ahwazi against this scholar. Finally, he emphasizes the scholar's well-known defense of tawhid and divine transcendence (tanzih) from anthropomorphism (tashbih) and limitation (tahdid), following the path of al-Ash'ari in usul al-din.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the scholar (Abu at-Tayyib's family) supported anthropomorphism (tashbih) or limitation (tahdid) of Allah.
Correction: The passage states they were well-known for exalting Allah from tashbih and tahdid, defending tawhid, and following al-Ash'ari.

Checkpoint
Which three groups of innovators did the family of Abu at-Tayyib struggle against in Nishapur?
A) Mu'tazila, B) Rafida, C) Karramiyya, D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school was actively defended by a family of Shafi'i scholars in Nishapur against Mu'tazila, Rafida, and Karramiyya, refuting false accusations through their consistent defense of tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own context, are you willing to stand up for your beliefs even if it means a long struggle against multiple opposed groups, as the family of Abu at-Tayyib did? What specific compromise or silence are you tempted by that goes against tawhid?
?
The passage shows that the family's defense was rooted in exalting God from anthropomorphism. Have you ever imagined God in human terms? What step will you take today to purify your concept of tawhid based on this lesson?
?
A false accusation was refuted by the scholar's consistent record. When people misunderstand or slander you, does your life speak clearly enough to refute it? What area of your character needs greater consistency so that your actions match your claimed beliefs?

Biography of Abu Nu'aym al-Istarabadi
Ibn Asakir provides a biographical notice on Abu Nu'aym al-Istarabadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details and virtues of the hadith scholar Abu Nu'aym al-Istarabadi.

Core Idea
Abu Nu'aym's life exemplifies the pious dedication of early hadith scholars.

This lesson presents a brief biography of Abu Nu'aym al-Istarabadi, a prominent hadith memorizer and supporter of the Sunni tradition, as recorded by Ibn Asakir. The passage highlights his learning journey, scholarly reputation, and his role in upholding the Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to understand the overall content.
Focus on the chain of transmission and the description of his qualities.
2
Identify the chain and key qualities
Trace the narration from the author back to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi. Notice the virtues attributed: truthfulness, piety, precision, vigilance.
3
Note the author's personal testimony
The author ends with 'I say: He used to support the Sunna in Jurjan.' This shows his own endorsement and the regional context.
This connects to the broader theme of upholding the Sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاما أبو نعيم الاستراباذي فهو عبدالملك الجرجاني الفقيه، قال لنا أبو الحسين على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني بدمشق وأبو منصور عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن عبد الواحد بن زريق الشيباني ببغداد، قال لنا أبو بكر أحمد بن على بن ثابت الخطيب إنه كان أحد أئمة المسلمين ومن الحفاظ في الشرائع والدين مع الحفاظ في الشرائع والدين مع صدق وتورع وضبط وتيقظ، سافر الكثير وكتب بالعراق والحجاز والشام ومصر ومات حدود سنة عشرين وثلثمائة قلت وكان ينصر السنة بجرجان.
As for Abu Nu'aym al-Istarabadi, he is Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani the faqih. He said to us: Abu al-Husayn Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani in Damascus and Abu Mansur Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Zurayq al-Shaybani in Baghdad. They said to us: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib [said]: He was one of the imams of the Muslims and among the memorizers of the shar'i sciences and religion, with truthfulness, piety, precision, and vigilance. He traveled extensively and wrote in Iraq, Hijaz, Syria, and Egypt, and he died around the year 320 AH. I say: He used to support the Sunna in Jurjan.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice about Abu Nu'aym (Abd al-Malik al-Jurjani), praising his stature as a hadith memorizer and his travels to collect knowledge. The author cites a chain of narrators to al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, who attested to his qualities. The author adds his own comment that Abu Nu'aym supported the Sunna in Jurjan.

Correction: They refer to the same person; he was from Istarbad, a town near Jurjan.
